Strangulation and Qisas: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for strangulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding qisas for death by strangulation, and identify the condition regarding duration that affects the ruling.

Core Idea
Strangulation does not always trigger qisas; Abu Hanifa denies it, Sahibayn require continuous fatal strangling.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether strangulation warrants qisas (retaliatory execution). Abu Hanifa holds that qisas is not applicable, but if the perpetrator habitually strangles, the ruler may execute him as a discretionary punishment. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue that if the strangling continues until death, qisas is obligatory. The text also clarifies a crucial nuance: if the strangler releases the victim before death, the duration of strangulation must be examined to determine if it was normally lethal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that the three eponymous Hanafi imams differ on qisas for strangulation. Abu Hanifa's view is contrasted with that of the Sahibayn.
This is an intra-madhhab dispute, not between schools.
2
State each position clearly
Abu Hanifa: 'no qisas upon him' (لا قصاص عليه). Sahibayn: if he continued strangling until death, 'qisas is upon him' (فعليه القصاص).
3
Examine the Sahibayn's analogy
They analogize strangulation to killing with a large stone or wood – both are direct fatal acts. The implicit illa is 'direct lethal force causing death'.
The opposing dalil is qiyas jali.
4
Apply the nuance condition
If the strangler stops before death and the victim dies later, examine the duration: if it was insufficient to cause death normally, no qisas even for Sahibayn.
This condition is agreed upon by all.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the victim's family cannot demand qisas; the ruler may only impose ta'zir (if habitual). Under Sahibayn, they can demand qisas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا جرح رجل حتى مات فعلى قول أبي حنيفة لا قصاص عليه ولكن إن اعتاد ذلك فالإمام يقتله حد وهو الساحر إذا تاب، وأمنا على قولهما إن دام على الخنق حتى مات فعليه القصاص كما لو قتله بحجر عظيم أو خشبة عظيمة . وإن كان ترك الخنق قبل الموت ثم مات بعد ذلك فإنه ينظر؛ إن دام على الخنق مقداراً لا يموت الإنسان منه غالباً فلا قصاص.
If a man wounds [strangles?] another so that he dies, according to Abu Hanifa there is no qisas upon him, but if he made a habit of it, the Imam executes him as a prescribed punishment (hadd), like a sorcerer if he repents. According to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], if he continued strangling until death, qisas is upon him, just as if he killed him with a large stone or a large piece of wood. If he stopped strangling before death and then he died after that, then it is examined: if he continued strangling for a period from which a person does not generally die, then no qisas.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on strangulation causing death. Abu Hanifa holds that qisas (retaliatory execution) is not applicable; however, if the person habitually engages in such dangerous acts, the ruler can execute him as a ta'zir (discretionary punishment) likened to the hadd for sorcery. His two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that if the strangulation is continuous until death, qisas is obligatory. The text then clarifies a nuance: if the strangler releases the victim before death and the victim later dies, the duration of the strangulation matters. If the duration was insufficient to cause death in most cases, no qisas. The example of killing with a stone or wood shows that the Sahibayn analogize strangulation to direct lethal blows.

Key Terms
خنق (khanq): Strangling, grasping the throat to prevent breathing.
حد (ḥadd): A fixed, divinely ordained punishment; here used for the ruler's discretionary execution of a habitual strangler.
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory punishment, specifically retribution in kind for homicide or injury.
تعزير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion, for acts not subject to hadd or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn, when is qisas obligatory for strangulation?
A) Only if the strangler uses a weapon.
B) Only if the victim is a minor.
C) If the strangler continues strangling until death, analogous to killing with a stone.
D) Only if the strangler confesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, strangulation does not automatically trigger qisas; the ruling depends on continuity and lethality, with Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differing on the basic obligation.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas Between Free and Slave: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on qisas between free and slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas between free and slave, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument from the verse 'al-hurr bi al-hurr', and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the concept of 'lam al-'ahd' and general texts.

Core Idea
The free is killed for the slave because inviolability is equal, and the verse 'al-hurr bi al-hurr' was for a specific incident.

One of the most famous inter-madhhab disputes in qisas is whether a free person is executed for intentionally killing a slave. Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions hold that the free is killed, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds otherwise. The disagreement turns on how to reconcile general verses commanding qisas for all lives with a specific verse that appears to match free with free and slave with slave. In this lesson, you will follow the Hanafi argument that the specific verse refers to a historical incident and does not override the general rule.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that a free person is executed for killing a slave (and also for a free person).
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues from the verse 'al-hurr bi al-hurr wa al-abd bi al-abd' that qisas requires matching of status, and a free person is not equal to a slave.
He also adds that slaves are property and thus not equal in dignity.
3
Identify the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi school relies on general texts: 'al-nafs bi al-nafs' (al-Ma'idah 5:45), 'kutiba alaykum al-qisas fi al-qatla' (al-Baqarah 2:178), and the hadith 'al-amdu qawad'. These all require qisas for intentional killing without distinction.
These are considered 'amm (general) and qat'i (definitive) in transmission.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i verse
The verse 'al-hurr bi al-hurr' is interpreted as referring to a specific historical incident (between Banu al-Nadhir and Banu Qurayza) where the stronger tribe demanded unequal compensation. The 'lam' in 'al-hurr' is 'lam al-'ahd' (for a known referent), not 'lam al-jins' (generic). Therefore, it does not restrict the general rule.
Ibn Abbas (RA) is cited as the source for this historical context.
5
Appreciate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Hanafi, the free killer is executed; according to Shafi'i, he is not executed but must pay diya (blood money) and possibly serve other penalties.
This difference has significant legal implications in cases of intentional homicide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وقتل الحر بالحر (وبالعبد) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : لا يقتل الحر بالعبد لقوله تعالى الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۷۸] فهذا يقتضي مقابلة الجنس بالجنس، ومن ضرورة المقابلة أن لا يقتل الحر بالعبد، ولأن القصاص يقتضي المساواة ولا مساواة بينهما إذ الحر مالك والعبد مملوك والمالكية أمارة القدرة والمملوكية أمارة العجز . ولنا العمومات نحو قوله تعالى وكتبنا عليهم فيها أن النفس بالنفس ﴾ [المائدة: ٤٥] وقوله تعالى كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى [البقرة : ۱۷۸] وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «العمد قود» ولا يعارض بما تلي لأن فيه مقابلة مقيدة وفيما تلونا مقابلة مطلقاً فلا يحمل على المقيد على أن مقابلة الحر بالحر لا تنافي الحر بالعبد لأنه ليس فيه إلا ذلك لبعض ما شمله العموم على موافقة حكمه وذلك لا يوجب تخصيص ما بقي ألا ترى أنه قابل الأنثى بالأنثى دليل على جريان القصاص بين الحرة والأمة وفائدة هذه المقابلة في الآية على ما قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما كانت بين النضير وبني قريظة مقابلة وكانوا بنوا قريظة أقل عدداً والنضير أشرف عندهم فتراضوا على أن العبد من بني النضير بمقابلة الحر من بني قريظة، والأنثى منهم بمقابلة الذكر من بني قريظة فأنزل الله تعالى الآية رداً عليهم وبياناً على أن الجنس يقتل بجنسه على اختلاف مواضعتهم من القبيلتين جميعاً فكانت اللام لتعريف العهد لا لتعريف الجنس، ولأنهما مستويان في العصمة إذ هي بالدين عنده وبالدار عندنا فيجري القصاص بينهما حسماً لمادة الفساد وتحقيقاً لمعنى الزجر ، ولو اعتبرت المساواة في غير العصمة في النفس لما جرى القصاص بين الذكر والأنثى، والقصاص يجب باعتبار أنه آدمي ولم يدخل في الملك من هذا الوجه بل هو منفي على أصل الحرية من هذا الوجه ولهذا يقتل العبد بالعبد، وكذا يقتل العبد بالحر ، ولو كان مالاً لما قتل. وكذلك عجزه وموته وبقاء أثر كفره حكمي فلا يؤثر ذلك في سقوط العصمة ولا يؤثر شبهة، ولو أورث شبهة لما جرى القصاص بين العبيد بعضهم ببعض . ووجوب القصاص في الأطراف يعتمد المساواة في الجزء المبان بعد المساواة في العصمة ولهذا لا تقطع الصحيح بالشلاء، وفي النفس لا يشترط ذلك حتى يقتل الصحيح بالزمن والمفلوج ولا مساواة بين أطراف الحر والعبد لا في العصمة فأظهر أن أثر الرق فيها دون النفس لما أن العبد من حيث النفس آدمي مكلف خلق معصوماً.
He (the author) said: A free person is killed for a free person (and for a slave). Al-Shafi'i said: A free person is not killed for a slave because of the verse: 'A free for a free, and a slave for a slave.' This implies matching of kind to kind, and from the necessity of matching is that a free person is not killed for a slave. Also because qisas requires equality, and there is no equality between them: the free is a possessor and the slave is possessed – possession indicates power and being possessed indicates helplessness. Our proof is the general texts: 'We prescribed for them therein: a life for a life,' and 'Prescribed for you is qisas in the case of killing,' and the Prophet's saying 'Intentional killing is qisas.' This is not contradicted by what was recited because it contains restricted matching, while we have unrestricted matching, so the unrestricted is not restricted to the restricted. Moreover, matching a free with a free does not negate free with slave because the verse only mentions that for some of what the general includes, and that does not necessitate specification of the rest. Do you not see that it matched female with female, which is evidence for qisas between free woman and slave woman? The benefit of this matching in the verse, according to Ibn Abbas (RA), is that there was a conflict between Banu al-Nadhir and Banu Qurayza; Banu Qurayza were fewer in number and Banu al-Nadhir were more noble in their view, so they agreed that a slave of Banu al-Nadhir would be matched to a free of Banu Qurayza, and a female of theirs to a male of Banu Qurayza. So Allah revealed the verse in rejection of them and as a clarification that the kind is killed by its kind according to their different positions from both tribes. Thus, the 'lam' is for 'ahd (specific reference), not for jins (generic). Also, the two are equal in inviolability, for it is by religion according to him and by residence according to us, so qisas runs between them to prevent corruption and fulfill the meaning of deterrence. If equality in matters other than inviolability in the life were considered, qisas would not run between male and female. Qisas is obligatory by virtue of being human, and from this aspect, he has not entered into ownership; rather, from this aspect it is negated based on the principle of freedom. For this reason, a slave is killed for a slave, and also a slave is killed for a free. If he were property, he would not be killed. Likewise, his incapacity, death, and traces of his disbelief are legal [effects], so they do not affect the dropping of inviolability, nor do they create a doubt. If it created a doubt, qisas would not run among slaves for one another. The obligation of qisas in limbs depends on equality in the part severed after equality in inviolability; for this reason, a healthy limb is not cut for a paralyzed one. In the case of life, this condition is not required, so a healthy person is killed for a chronically ill and a paralyzed one. There is no equality between limbs of free and slave in inviolability, so it is apparent that the effect of slavery is greater in limbs than in life, because a slave, in terms of life, is a responsible human created inviolable.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether a free person is executed for intentionally killing a slave. The author states the Hanafi position: a free person is killed for a slave (and for a free person). Imam al-Shafi'i opposes this, arguing from the verse 'a free for a free, a slave for a slave,' which he interprets as requiring matching of status, and from the principle of equality in qisas. The Hanafi response is based on general Qur'anic texts like 'a life for a life' and 'qisas is prescribed for you in the case of killing,' and the hadith 'al-amdu qawad' (intentional killing is qisas). They argue that the verse in al-Baqarah is specific to a historical incident between two tribes and does not negate the general rule. Moreover, the slave and free are equal in ismah (inviolability) because the slave is a human, not property in this regard. The Hanafi school thus extends qisas between free and slave based on the general principle, while the Shafi'i restricts it. The passage also distinguishes between qisas for limbs (which require equality of the part) and for life (which does not). This is a critical refinement of the Hanafi position against Shafi'i.

Key Terms
عصمة (ismah): Inviolability of life; the legal protection against killing.
مقابلة (muqabalah): Matching or pairing in the Qur'anic text; here the Shafi'i argument that the verse pairs free with free, slave with slave, implying non-matching categories.
لام العهد (lam al-'ahd): The definite article used for a specific known referent (a particular group or incident), as opposed to lam al-jins (generic).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why does the verse 'al-hurr bi al-hurr wa al-abd bi al-abd' not prevent qisas of a free person for a slave?
A) Because the verse is abrogated (mansukh) by earlier revelations.
B) Because the 'lam' in 'al-hurr' is for 'ahd (specific reference), not for jins (generic).
C) Because the verse only applies to cases where the killer is a slave.
D) Because Abu Hanifa rejected the authenticity of that verse.

Key Takeaway
The free is killed for the slave because inviolability (ismah) is equal, and the verse 'al-hurr bi al-hurr' is specific to a historical incident, not a general restriction.

Qisas of a Free Man for a Slave
Hanafi ruling and proof that a free man is executed for killing a slave, with response to Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a free man is executed for killing a slave, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
A free man is killed for a slave because inviolability (ʻiṣma) is based on being human, not on ownership.

This passage presents a crucial inter-madhhab dispute in qisas. The Hanafi school holds that a free man who intentionally kills a slave is subject to qisas, meaning the victim's owner can demand execution. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing from the Quranic verse 'the free for the free, the slave for the slave.' The Hanafis respond with general texts and a contextual interpretation of that verse. Understanding this dispute illuminates deeper principles: how general and specific texts interact, the basis of inviolability (ʻiṣma), and the role of equality in qisas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and the Shafi'i objection
Identify the exact positions: Hanafi says free man is killed for slave; Shafi'i says he is not. This is the axis of the dispute.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Study the Shafi'i dalil: Quran 2:178 'the free for the free...' and the argument that qisas requires equality (musawah) which is lacking between owner and owned.
3
Analyse the Hanafi evidence
Review the general texts cited: Quran 5:45 'a life for a life', 2:178 'prescribed is qisas', and the hadith 'al-ʻamdu qawad'. Understand why these are taken as unrestricted ('amm).
4
Understand the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafis interpret the specific verse as contextual (Banu al-Nadir vs Banu Qurayzah) via Ibn 'Abbas, and argue that the general texts prevail. Also note the Hanafi view that ʻiṣma is equal in life for free and slave.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Hanafi law, the owner can demand execution; under Shafi'i, only diyah is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وقتل الحر بالحر (وبالعبد) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : لا يقتل الحر بالعبد لقوله تعالى الحر بالحر والعبد بالعبد ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۷۸] فهذا يقتضي مقابلة الجنس بالجنس، ومن ضرورة المقابلة أن لا يقتل الحر بالعبد، ولأن القصاص يقتضي المساواة ولا مساواة بينهما إذ الحر مالك والعبد مملوك والمالكية أمارة القدرة والمملوكية أمارة العجز . ولنا العمومات نحو قوله تعالى وكتبنا عليهم فيها أن النفس بالنفس ﴾ [المائدة: ٤٥] وقوله تعالى كتب عليكم القصاص في القتلى [البقرة : ۱۷۸] وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «العمد قود» ولا يعارض بما تلي لأن فيه مقابلة مقيدة وفيما تلونا مقابلة مطلقاً فلا يحمل على المقيد على أن مقابلة الحر بالحر لا تنافي الحر بالعبد لأنه ليس فيه إلا ذلك لبعض ما شمله العموم على موافقة حكمه وذلك لا يوجب تخصيص ما بقي ألا ترى أنه قابل الأنثى بالأنثى دليل على جريان القصاص بين الحرة والأمة وفائدة هذه المقابلة في الآية على ما قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما كانت بين النضير وبني قريظة مقابلة وكانوا بنوا قريظة أقل عدداً النضير أشرف عندهم فتراضوا على أن العبد من بني النضير بمقابلة الحر من بني قريظة، والأنثى منهم بمقابلة الذكر من بني قريظة فأنزل الله تعالى الآية رداً عليهم وبياناً على أن الجنس يقتل بجنسه على اختلاف مواضعتهم من القبيلتين جميعاً فكانت اللام لتعريف العهد لا لتعريف الجنس، ولأنهما مستويان في العصمة إذ هي بالدين عنده وبالدار عندنا فيجري القصاص بينهما حسماً لمادة الفساد وتحقيقاً لمعنى الزجر ، ولو اعتبرت المساواة في غير العصمة في النفس لما جرى القصاص بين الذكر والأنثى، والقصاص يجب باعتبار أنه آدمي ولم يدخل في الملك من هذا الوجه جه بل هو منفي على أصل الحرية من هذا الوجه ولهذا يقتل العبد بالعبد، وكذا يقتل العبد بالحر ، ولو كان مالاً لما قتل. وكذلك عجزه وموته وبقاء أثر كفره حكمي فلا يؤثر ذلك في سقوط العصمة ولا يؤثر شبهة، ولو أورث شبهة لما جرى القصاص بين العبيد بعضهم ببعض . ووجوب القصاص في الأطراف يعتمد المساواة في الجزء المبان بعد المساواة في العصمة ولهذا لا تقطع الصحيح بالشلاء، وفي النفس لا يشترط ذلك حتى يقتل الصحيح بالزمن والمفلوج ولا مساواة بين أطراف الحر والعبد لا في العصمة فأظهر أن أثر الرق فيها دون النفس لما أن العبد من حيث النفس آدمي مكلف خلق معصوماً.
He (the author) said: And killing a free man for a free man (and for a slave). Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: A free man is not killed for a slave because of His statement 'The free for the free, and the slave for the slave' [Quran 2:178]. This necessitates matching genus with genus, and from the necessary consequence of matching is that a free man is not killed for a slave. And because qisas requires equality, and there is no equality between them since the free man is an owner and the slave is owned, and ownership is an indication of ability while being owned is an indication of incapacity. Our evidence is the general texts such as His statement 'And We prescribed for them therein that a life for a life' [Quran 5:45] and His statement 'Prescribed for you is legal retribution for the murdered' [Quran 2:178] and his statement (peace be upon him) 'Intentional killing is qisas.' And it is not contradicted by what was recited, because that is a restricted matching while what we recited is an unrestricted matching, so it is not interpreted restrictively. Moreover, the matching of free with free does not negate free with slave, because it only includes that which is covered by the general ruling in accordance with its rule, and that does not necessitate specification of what remains. Do you not see that He matched female with female, indicating qisas between a free woman and a slave woman. And the benefit of this matching in the verse, according to Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them), was that there was a conflict between Banu al-Nadir and Banu Qurayzah: Banu Qurayzah were fewer in number but Banu al-Nadir were nobler in their view, so they agreed that a slave from Banu al-Nadir would be matched with a free man from Banu Qurayzah, and a female from them with a male from Banu Qurayzah. So Allah sent down the verse as a refutation of them and an explanation that the genus is killed by its genus despite the difference in their positions from both tribes. Thus the laam is for definition of the covenant, not for definition of the genus. And because both are equal in inviolability (ʻiṣma), for it is by religion according to him (al-Shafi'i) and by abode (dar) according to us, so qisas is executed between them to cut off corruption and to achieve deterrence. If equality were considered in other than inviolability regarding the life, then qisas would not apply between male and female. And qisas is obligatory on the basis that he is a human being, and ownership does not enter from this aspect; rather, it is negated on the principle of freedom from this aspect. For this reason, a slave is killed for a slave, and likewise a slave is killed for a free man. And if he were property, he would not be killed. Similarly, his impotence, death, and the remnant of his disbelief are legal matters that do not affect the inviolability, nor does a doubt affect it. And if it had caused doubt, then qisas would not apply among slaves themselves. The obligation of qisas in limbs depends on equality in the severed part after equality in inviolability; thus a healthy limb is not cut for a paralyzed one. But in life, that is not required, so a healthy person is killed for a sick or paralyzed one. And there is no equality between the limbs of a free man and a slave in inviolability; rather, it is apparent that the effect of slavery is in the limbs, not in the life, because the slave is, in terms of life, a human being, responsible, created inviolable.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author states the Hanafi ruling that a free man is executed in qisas for killing a slave, and then presents the Shafi'i objection. Al-Shafi'i argues that the Quranic verse 'the free for the free, the slave for the slave' implies matching within each category, so a free man cannot be killed for a slave. He also argues that qisas requires equality (musawah) and there is no equality because a free man is an owner and a slave is owned. The Hanafi response uses general texts: the Quran says 'a life for a life' (Quran 5:45) and 'prescribed for you is qisas for the murdered' (Quran 2:178), and the hadith 'intentional killing is qisas.' These are unrestricted, so the restricted verse (free for free, slave for slave) is interpreted as a specific historical context (between Banu al-Nadir and Banu Qurayzah) according to Ibn 'Abbas, not as a general rule. The Hanafis argue that inviolability (ʻiṣma) is equal in both free and slave because it is based on being a human being (adami) and the dar (abode) in the Hanafi view (since dhimmah is based on residence). Thus qisas applies to preserve deterrence and prevent corruption. The author also contrasts limb qisas: limbs require equality in the severed part (so a healthy limb is not cut for a paralyzed one), but life does not require such equality, so a healthy person is executed for a sick or paralyzed victim. The conclusion is that slavery does not affect the inviolability of life; the slave is a responsible human being created with ʻiṣma.

Key Terms
العصمة (al-ʻiṣma): Inviolability or legal protection of life and property; the quality that makes one's blood and property unlawful to violate.
القود (al-qawad): Retaliation, specifically qisas for intentional killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does a free man get executed for killing a slave despite the verse 'the free for the free, the slave for the slave'?
A) The verse is abrogated by the general verses.
B) The verse was revealed for a specific historical context and does not restrict the general rules.
C) Slaves are considered property, so qisas is not required.
D) The free man's family must consent before execution.

Key Takeaway
A free man is executed for killing a slave in Hanafi law because the inviolability of life is equal for all humans, regardless of ownership status.

Qisas of a Muslim for a Dhimmi
Hanafi position on qisas for a Muslim killing a dhimmi, with refutation of Shafi'i's hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qisas for a Muslim who kills a dhimmi, evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi methodology of interpreting the hadith to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's life is fully inviolable like a Muslim's under Hanafi law – the Prophet himself executed a Muslim for killing a dhimmi.

This lesson addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: should a Muslim be executed in qisas for killing a dhimmi? The Hanafi school says yes, based on the principle that the covenant of dhimmah grants full inviolability. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing the hadith 'A Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever, nor a person of covenant in his covenant.' By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Hanafi school reconciles its position with that hadith through careful istidlal and grammatical analysis.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the Hanafi school regarding qisas for a Muslim who kills a dhimmi.
The ruling is that qisas is wajib, just as if the victim were a Muslim.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Which school disagrees and what is their primary dalil from hadith?
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith narrated by 'Ali: 'A Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever, nor a person of covenant in his covenant.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing dalil
How do Hanafis interpret this hadith? What counter-narratives do they present?
They argue the hadith refers to a harbi, not a dhimmi, and the Prophet's own action contradicts a strict reading.
4
Examine the underlying principle: ismah
Why do Hanafis consider a dhimmi fully inviolable? What evidence supports full ismah?
Evidence includes qisas between dhimmis, cutting the hand for stealing a dhimmi's property, and the saying of 'Ali.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings between the two schools?
Hanafi: qisas possible; Shafi'i: only diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والمسلم بالذمي) يعني يقتل المسلم بالذمي. وقال الشافعي : لا يقتل به لما أخرجه علي بن أبي طالب عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال لا يقتل مسلم بكافر ولا ذو عهد في عهده»(۱) الحديث ولنا ما تلونا من كتاب الله وما روينا من السنة فإنه بإطلاقه يتناوله، وقد صح عن عبد الرحمن ابن سلمة ومحمد بن المنكدر أن رسول الله الله أتى برجل من المسلمين قد قتل معاهداً من أهل الذمة فأمر به فضرب عنقه فقال : أنا أولى من وافي بذمته، والقصاص يعتمد العصمة على ما بينا في العبد وقد وجدت نظراً إلى الدار وإلى التكليف، ولأن شرط التكليف القدرة على ما كلف به ولا يتمكن من إقامة ما كلف به إلا يدفع أسباب الهلاك عنه، وذلك بأن يكون محرم التعرض ولا نسلم أن الكفر مبيح بنفسه بلا بواسطة الحراب ألا ترى أن من لا يقاتل منهم لا يحل قتله كالشيخ الفاني وقد اندفع الحراب بعقد الذمة فكان معصوماً بلا شبهة ولهذا يقتل الذمي بالذمي ولو كان في عصمته خلل لما قتل الذمي بالذمي كما لا يقتل المستأمن بالمستأمن وقد قال علي رضي الله عنه : إنما بذلوا الجزية لتكون دماؤهم كدمائنا وأموالهم كأموالنا . وذلك بأن تكون معصومة بلا شبهة كالمسلم ولهذا يقطع المسلم بسرقة مال الذمي، ولو كانت في عصمته شبهة لما قطع كما لا يقطع في سرقة مال المستأمن لأن المال تبع للنفس وأمر المال أهون من النفس، فلما قطع بسرقته كان أولى أن يقتل بقتله لأن أمر النفس أعظم من المال ألا تری أن العبد لا يقطع بسرقة مال مولاه ويقتل بقتل مولاه لما ذكرنا، والذي يدلك على ما قلنا أن الذمي لو قتل ذمياً ثم أسلم القاتل قبل أن يقتل قتل به فعلم أن المراد به الحربي إذ هو لا يقتل به مسلم ولا ذمي ولا يقال معناه لا يقتل ذو عهد مطلقاً أي لا يحل قتله فيكون ابتداء كلام لأنا نقول : هذا لا يستقيم لوجهين: أحدهما أن ذا عهد مفرد وقد عطف على جملة فيأخذ الحكم منها لأن المعطوف الناقص يأخذ الحكم من المعطوف عليه التام كما يقال قام زيد وعمرو أو يقال قتل زيد بعمرو وخالد أي كلاهما قام أو قتل، ولا يجوز أن يقدر له خبر آخر والظاهر أن المعنى يأبى ذلك لأن المراد بسوق الكلام الأول نفي القتل قصاصاً لا نفي مطلق القتل فكذا الثاني تحقيقاً للعطف إذ لا يجوز ذلك ألبتة في المفرد ألا ترى إلى قوله تعالى وما يستوي الأعمى والبصير [فاطر: ۱۹] أن المنفي الاستواء في البصر والعمى لا في كل وصف ولهذا أجرى القصاص بينهما لاستوائهما في العصمة، وكذا نقصان حال الكافر بكفره لا يزيل عصمته فلا عبرة به كسائر الأوصاف الناقصة كالشلل والأنوثة، ولا نسلم أن كفره مبيح للقتل بلا حرابه هو المبيح وقد ذكرناه غيره مرة بخلاف ما الملك والأخت من الرضاع فإنه مبيح للوطء، وإنما امتنع في الأخت المذكورة ذكر من بعارض فأورث شبهة . (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الديات باب ٢٤ ، ٣١ أبو داود في كتاب الديات باب ١١. الترمذي في كتاب الديات باب ١٦. ابن ماجه في كتاب الديات باب .۲۱ أحمد في مسنده (۱/ ۷۹. ۱۱۹).
He (the author) said: (And the Muslim for the dhimmi), meaning the Muslim is killed for the dhimmi. Al-Shafi'i said: He is not killed for him because of what 'Ali ibn Abi Talib narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he said: 'A Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever, nor a person of covenant in his covenant.' (Hadith) Our evidence is what we recited from the Book of Allah and what we narrated from the Sunnah, for it includes him by its generality. And it is authentic from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Salamah and Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was brought a Muslim man who had killed a covenanted person from the people of dhimmah, so he ordered him and struck his neck and said: 'I am the most entitled of those who fulfill their covenant.' Qisas is based on inviolability as we explained regarding the slave, and it is found by considering the abode (dar) and the capacity (taklif). And because the condition of taklif is ability to do what one is commanded, and one cannot fulfill what he is commanded unless he repels causes of destruction from himself, and that is by being forbidden to be assaulted. And we do not accept that disbelief itself permits killing without the intermediary of harb (hostility). Do you not see that those who do not fight among them are not permissible to kill, like the elderly decrepit? And harb is removed by the covenant of dhimmah, so he is inviolable without doubt. For this reason, a dhimmi is killed for a dhimmi, and if there were a defect in his inviolability, a dhimmi would not be killed for a dhimmi, just as a musta'min is not killed for a musta'min. And 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'They paid jizyah so that their blood would be like our blood and their wealth like our wealth.' And that means they should be inviolable without doubt like a Muslim. For this reason, a Muslim's hand is cut off for stealing the property of a dhimmi, and if there were a doubt in his inviolability, it would not be cut off, just as it is not cut off for stealing the property of a musta'min, because property follows the person, and the matter of property is less serious than the person. Since it is cut off for stealing it, it is more appropriate that he should be killed for killing him, because the matter of life is greater than property. Do you not see that a slave's hand is not cut off for stealing his master's property, but he is killed for killing his master, as we mentioned. What indicates to you what we said is that if a dhimmi kills a dhimmi and then the killer becomes Muslim before being killed, he is killed for him. Thus it is known that what is meant (by the hadith) is the harbi (combatant disbeliever), for he is not killed for a Muslim or a dhimmi. And it is not said that its meaning is that a person of covenant is not killed at all, i.e., it is not permissible to kill him, making it an initial statement, because we say: This is not valid for two reasons. First, 'person of covenant' is singular and is conjoined to a sentence, so it takes the ruling from it, because an incomplete conjunct takes the ruling from the complete conjunct, as one says 'Zaid and 'Amr stood' or 'Zaid was killed for 'Amr and Khalid' meaning both stood or were killed. And it is not permissible to assume another predicate. And the apparent meaning rejects that because the intent of the first part of the speech is the negation of killing by way of qisas, not the absolute negation of killing; thus the second part is likewise for the sake of conjunct validity, and this is absolutely not permissible in the singular. Do you not see His statement 'And the blind and the seeing are not equal' [Quran 35:19] that what is negated is equality in sight and blindness, not in every description. Thus qisas is executed between them because of their equality in inviolability. Similarly, the deficiency of the disbeliever due to his disbelief does not remove his inviolability, so it is not considered, like other deficient attributes such as paralysis and femininity. And we do not accept that his disbelief permits killing without his harb (hostility); it is harb that permits it, and we have mentioned this elsewhere. This is unlike the case of a wife or a foster sister, where a particular attribute permits sexual intercourse, but it is prevented in the mentioned sister because of a conflicting cause that creates doubt.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author states the Hanafi ruling that a Muslim is executed in qisas for killing a dhimmi (a non-Muslim under Muslim protection). Al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing the hadith 'A Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever, nor a person of covenant in his covenant.' The Hanafi response first offers a counter-narrative: authentic reports that the Prophet himself ordered the execution of a Muslim who killed a dhimmi, saying 'I am the most entitled to fulfill the covenant.' Then they argue that qisas depends on inviolability (ʻiṣma), which a dhimmi possesses fully because of the covenant of dhimmah that removes the state of harb (hostility). A dhimmi is inviolable without doubt because he is subject to Islamic law (taklif) and pays jizyah in exchange for protection. This is proven by the fact that a dhimmi is killed for killing another dhimmi, showing complete ʻiṣma. If there were any doubt, qisas would not apply, just as it does not between musta'mins (temporary residents). Furthermore, the hand of a Muslim is cut off for stealing a dhimmi's property, and if life is more important than property, then qisas is even more justified. The hadith of 'Ali is interpreted to refer to a harbi disbeliever (one in a state of war), not a dhimmi. The conjunction in the hadith is analyzed grammatically: 'nor a person of covenant' is a conjunct to the first clause 'A Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever', and the context (narrative of qisas) indicates it means negation of qisas, not absolute prohibition of killing. The passage concludes by comparing disbelief to other deficient attributes like paralysis or femininity, which do not negate ʻiṣma. The only thing that permits killing is harb (active hostility), and that is removed by the dhimmah covenant.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule with a covenant (dhimmah) guaranteeing protection of life and property in exchange for jizyah.
المستأمن (al-musta'min): A non-Muslim given temporary safe passage (aman) into Muslim territory, whose ʻiṣma is temporary and limited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for considering a dhimmi's life fully inviolable for qisas?
A) The dhimmi's payment of jizyah
B) The covenant of dhimmah that removes harb
C) The Quranic verse 'a life for a life'
D) The hadith 'A Muslim is not killed for a disbeliever'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a Muslim is executed in qisas for killing a dhimmi because the covenant of dhimmah grants full inviolability, equal to that of a Muslim.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
10 min
Qisas and Musta'min: Equality in Blood Protection
Ruling with qiyas and istihsan reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for killing a musta'min and explain how qiyas and istihsan interact to produce the final ruling.

Core Idea
Equality in permanent blood protection is essential for qisas; a musta'min's temporary protection prevents retaliation.

In the Hanafi school, qisas is the default for intentional killing, but it requires equality in the inviolability of blood (ismah) between killer and victim. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why a Muslim or dhimmi is not executed for killing a musta'min (a temporary protected person from enemy territory). It also explores the hypothetical case of one musta'min killing another, where qiyas suggests qisas but istihsan overrides it. Understanding this illustrates the Hanafi method of balancing analogy and juristic preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the passage to find the explicit statement: a Muslim and a dhimmi are not killed for a musta'min. Note the reason given: the musta'min's blood is not permanently protected, so equality (musawah) is absent.
2
Understand the condition for qisas
Recognize that equality in ismah (blood protection) is a condition for qisas in the Hanafi school. Here, the musta'min's protection is temporary (due to aman), unlike the permanent protection of a Muslim or dhimmi.
3
Analyze the qiyas case
Consider the case of two musta'mins. The text says that by qiyas, qisas would apply because they are equal in protection (both have temporary protection). Identify the asl (two permanently protected persons) and the illa (equality in protection).
4
Apply istihsan
The text then says that by istihsan, qisas is not applied. The reason is the existence of a mubih (permissibility) – the temporary nature of the protection that makes the killing less severe. Understand that istihsan overrides qiyas here.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi method
Note that the Hanafi school uses both qiyas and istihsan, with istihsan prevailing. The final ruling is that qisas does not apply in either case (Muslim/dhimmi killing musta'min, or musta'min killing musta'min).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجنايات باب ما يوجب القصاص وما لا يوجبه
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يقتلان بمستأمن أي لا يقتل المسلم ولا الذمي بحربي دخل دارنا بأمان لأن دمه ليس بمحقون على التأبيد فانعدمت المساواة، وكذا كفره باعث على الحراب لقصده الرجوع إلى دار الحرب ويقتل المستأمن بالمستأمن قياساً لوجود المساواة بينهما ولا يقتل استحساناً لوجود المبيح.
The Book of Crimes, Chapter on What Mandates Qisas and What Does Not. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And the two are not killed for a musta'min, meaning a Muslim and a dhimmi are not killed for a harbi who entered our land with aman, because his blood is not permanently protected, so equality is absent. Likewise, his disbelief incites hostility because he intends to return to dar al-harb. The musta'min is killed for the musta'min by qiyas due to the existence of equality between them, but he is not killed by istihsan due to the existence of a permissibility.'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding qisas for a musta'min (a person with a safe-conduct). The author states that neither a Muslim nor a dhimmi is subject to qisas for killing a musta'min because the musta'min's blood is not permanently inviolable, so there is no equality in protection (ismah) between killer and victim—a prerequisite for qisas. Additionally, the musta'min's disbelief prompts hostility as he intends to return to enemy territory. The text then contrasts the case of one musta'min killing another: by qiyas (analogy), qisas would apply because both are equal in protection. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), qisas is not applied because there is a legal permissibility (mubih) that prevents it—the temporary nature of the musta'min's protection. The Hanafi school uses both qiyas and istihsan, with istihsan prevailing here.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A person from enemy territory who enters Muslim lands with a safe-conduct (aman), temporarily protected.
عصمة (ismah): Inviolability of blood; the legal protection that makes killing unlawful and requires qisas if violated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school apply istihsan to deny qisas between two musta'mins?
A) Because they are both polytheists
B) Because of the existence of a permissibility (mubih)
C) Because their protection is permanent
D) Because they intend to return to dar al-harb

Key Takeaway
Qisas requires equality in permanent blood protection; temporary protection (aman) negates qisas, even between two musta'mins, due to istihsan.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas Between Man and Woman, Adult and Child, etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the Hanafi school applies qisas between all persons with equal ismah, regardless of gender, age, health, or disability.

Core Idea
Qisas requires equality in ismah, not in physique or age.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a foundational Hanafi principle: qisas is valid between a man and a woman, an adult and a child, a healthy person and a blind, chronically ill, amputee, or insane person. The sole criterion is equality in blood inviolability (ismah). If other factors like physical strength were considered, qisas would rarely be possible, leading to social disorder.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the act and its ruling
The passage lists several pairs: man/woman, adult/child, healthy/blind, etc., and rules that the healthy man is killed for each of these victims. The ruling is that qisas applies.
2
2. Isolate the criterion for equality
The author explicitly states that qisas applies 'due to equality in ismah.' This is the only factor that matters for the validity of qisas.
3
3. Understand the counterfactual
If we considered other factors like strength, health, or age, the door of qisas would be closed and discord would appear. This demonstrates the necessity of the principle.
4
4. Apply the principle to other cases
Any two persons with equal ismah (both Muslim or both protected by dhimmah) can have qisas, regardless of physical differences. The criterion is purely legal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والرجل بالمرأة والكبير بالصغير والصحيح بالأعمى والزمن وناقص الأطراف وبالمجنون) يعني يقتل الرجل الصحيح بهؤلاء وهو معطوف على ما تقدم من قوله «وقتل الحر بالحر الخ» لا على ما يليه من قوله ولا يقتلان بمستأمن» وإنما جرى القصاص بينهم لوجود المساواة بينهم في العصمة والمساواة فيها هي المعبرة في هذا الباب، ولو اعتبرت فيما وراءها لا نسد باب القصاص ولظهر الفتن.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And a man for a woman, and an adult for a child, and a healthy person for a blind person, a chronically ill person, an amputee, and an insane person.' Meaning: a healthy man is killed for these persons. This is connected to what preceded, i.e., 'killing a free person for a free person, etc.,' not to what follows, i.e., 'and the two are not killed for a musta'min.' Qisas applies between them only because of the existence of equality between them in protection (ismah), and equality in protection is the consideration in this chapter. If other factors were considered, the door of qisas would be closed and discord would appear.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage establishes that qisas applies between various categories of people: a man for a woman, an adult for a child, a healthy person for a blind person, a chronically ill person, an amputee, and an insane person. The author explains that this is based on the principle of equality in ismah (blood inviolability). All these persons have equal protection of life, so qisas is valid regardless of physical differences. The author notes that if we considered other factors (like strength, health, etc.), qisas would rarely apply, leading to social disorder. The ruling is straightforward and without dispute in this text.

Key Terms
العصمة (al-ismah): Legal inviolability of blood; the quality that makes one's life protected and killing unlawful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No, because qisas only applies between equals in every respect

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, qisas is based solely on equality in ismah, so it applies between all protected persons regardless of physical differences.

Qisas — Retaliation

Parent-Child Qisas: Father Not Killed for Child
Ruling that a child is killed for a parent but a parent is not killed for a child, with proof and rebuttal of Malik's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on qisas between parent and child, identify the Maliki objection, and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
A father is never killed for his child due to paternal mercy and the general hadith.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a sensitive area of Islamic criminal law: qisas between ascendants and descendants. The Hanafi school holds that a father is not subject to qisas for killing his child, even if the killing is deliberate, based on the hadith and the prevailing custom of paternal mercy. The Maliki school, however, distinguishes between killing by discipline and clear murder. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: a child is killed for a parent, but a parent is not killed for a child. Note the proof: the hadith 'لا يقاد الوالد بولده' and the reasoning of paternal mercy creating doubt (shubha).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that if the father kills by a clear murder method (e.g., slaughter), qisas applies because there is no doubt. But if by a blow, it may be discipline and no qisas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik analogizes to zina with a daughter: if a father commits zina with his daughter, he is stoned (rajm). Similarly, if he clearly murders his child, qisas should apply.
The analogy is based on the absence of doubt in both cases.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith is general and paternal mercy is the prevailing custom; rare exceptions do not change the rule. Zina is different because stoning is a pure divine right (haqq Allah), not a personal right like qisas.
The Hanafis emphasize the common custom (urf) of fathers not intentionally killing their children.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, a father never faces qisas for killing his child. Under Maliki law, he does if the killing is clearly murder (e.g., by slaughter). This practical difference affects judicial outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والولد بالوالد) لما تلونا وروينا من العمومات ولما ذكرنا من المعاني . قال رحمه الله : (ولا يقتل الرجل بالولد) لقوله عليه الصلاة السلام «لا يقاد الوالد بولده ولا السيد بعبده» (۱) ولأن الوالد لا يقتل ولده غالباً لوفور شفقته فيكون ذلك شبهة في سقوط القصاص، ولأن الأب لا يستحق العقوبة بولده لأن لأحيائه فمن المحال أن يكون الولد سبباً لإفنائه ولهذا لا يقتله إذا وجده في صف المشركين مقاتلاً أو زانياً وهو محصن، وهذا لأن القصاص يستحقه الوارث بسبب انعقد للميت خلافه ولو قتل به كان القاتل هو الابن نيابة وطولب بالفرق بين هذا وبين من زنى بابنته وهو محصن فإنه يرجم . أجيب بأن الرجم حق الله على الخصوص بخلاف القصاص؛ لا يقال فيجب أن يحد إذا زنى بجارية ابنه لأنا نقول: ثبت له حق الملك بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «أنت ومالك لأبيك (۲) . قال رحمه الله : ( والأم والجد والجدة كالأب) سواء كان من جهة الأب أو . جهة الأم لأنه جزؤهم فالنص الوارد في الأب يكون وارداً فيهم دلالة فكانت الشبهة شاملة للجميع في جميع صور القتل. وقال مالك رحمه الله تعالى : إن قتله ضرباً بالسيف فلا قصاص عليه لاحتمال أنه قصد تأديبه، وإن كان ذبحه ذبحاً فعليه القصاص لأنه عمد لا شبهة فيه ولا تأويل بل جناية الأب أغلظ لأن فيه قطع الرحم . فصار كمن زنی بابنته حيث يرجم كما لو زنی بالأجنبية . والحجة عليه ما روينا وما بينا وليس هذا كالزنا ببنته لأن الأب لوفور شفقته يجتنب ما يضر ولده بل يتحمل الضرر عنه حتى يسلم ولده فهذا هو العادة الفاشية بين الناس فلا يتوهم أن يقصد قتل ولده، فإن وجد ما يدل على ذلك فهو من العوارض النادرة فلا يتغير بذلك القواعد الشرعية ألا ترى أن السفر المشقة غالباً كان له أن يترخص برخصة المسافرين فلا يتغير ذلك بما يتفق فيه لبعضهم من الراحة ولا كذلك الزنا.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And a child for a parent' due to the generalities we recited and narrated and the meanings we mentioned. He said: 'And a man is not killed for a child' because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'A parent is not executed for his child, nor a master for his slave.' And because the parent does not usually kill his child due to abundant mercy, so that is a doubt (shubha) causing the dropping of qisas. And because the father does not deserve punishment through his child, for his living? It is impossible that the child be a cause of his annihilation; hence he is not killed if he finds him fighting in the ranks of the polytheists or committing zina while being muhsan. This is because qisas is deserved by the heir due to what is established for the deceased otherwise, and if he were killed by it, the killer would be the son by proxy. And he demanded a distinction between this and one who commits zina with his daughter while being muhsan, in which case he is stoned. It was answered: Stoning is a right of Allah specifically, unlike qisas. Do not say: Then he must be hadd if he commits zina with his son's slave-girl, for we say: He has ownership right established by his statement, peace be upon him: 'You and your property belong to your father.' He said: 'And the mother, grandfather, and grandmother are like the father,' whether from the father's side or mother's side because they are parts of him; thus the text concerning the father applies to them by implication, so the doubt encompasses all in all forms of killing. And Malik (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If he killed him by hitting with a sword, there is no qisas upon him because it is possible he intended discipline. If he slaughtered him, then qisas is upon him because it is premeditated with no doubt or interpretation; rather the father's crime is more severe because it severs kinship. So it becomes like one who commits zina with his daughter, where he is stoned as if he committed zina with a foreign woman. The argument against him is what we narrated and explained, and this is not like zina with his daughter because the father, due to abundant mercy, avoids harming his child and rather bears harm for him so that the child is safe. This is the prevalent custom among people, so it is not imagined that he intends to kill his child. If evidence indicates that, it is a rare occurrence, so legal rules do not change thereby. Do you not see that travel is predominantly hardship, so he may avail the concession of travellers, and that does not change due to some comfort occurring in it. And not so for zina.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage covers the Hanafi ruling on parent-child qisas. It states that a child is subject to qisas for killing a parent, but a parent is not subject to qisas for killing a child. The proof is the hadith: 'A parent is not executed for his child, nor a master for his slave.' The reasoning includes the father's natural mercy, creating a doubt (shubha) that prevents qisas. The mother, grandfather, and grandmother are included by analogy. The passage then presents the Maliki position: if the father kills by a blow with a sword, there is no qisas (likely discipline), but if he slaughters, qisas applies. The Hanafi response reiterates the hadith and the custom of parental mercy, emphasizing that this is the general rule and rare exceptions do not change it. The Malikis analogize to zina with a daughter, but the Hanafis distinguish because stoning is a pure divine right, while qisas involves a personal right of the victim's heir.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): Legal doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a severe penalty like qisas.
لا يقاد الوالد بولده (la yuqādu al-wālidu bi-waladihi): The prophetic hadith meaning 'A parent is not executed for his child'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does the mother also not face qisas for killing her child?
A) Because she is not an heir
B) Because she is included in the text about the father by implication, being a part of him
C) Because the hadith only mentions the father
D) Because women are never subject to qisas

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a parent is never subject to qisas for killing a child, based on the hadith and the presumption of paternal mercy, which creates a legal doubt (shubha) that blocks the penalty.

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas and Ownership: The Indivisibility Principle
Ruling on qisas with slaves and father

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas when the killer owns the victim (entirely or partially) and explain why qisas drops, applying the principle of indivisibility.

Core Idea
Qisas is indivisible: partial ownership drops it entirely because the owner cannot punish himself.

This lesson examines when qisas (retribution) is not applied despite an intentional killing. The Hanafi school rules that a person is not killed for killing his own slave or a slave he partially owns, nor does a son execute qisas against his father. The key principle is that qisas is indivisible (la yatajazzā) – if it cannot be fully applied due to ownership, it falls completely. We will explore the textual proof and the legal reasoning behind this exemption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
List all cases where qisas is negated: killing one's own slave, mudabbar, mukatab, son's slave, or a slave partially owned; also inheriting qisas against one's father. The ruling is that qisas drops in all these cases.
The passage explicitly names each scenario – note the pattern: ownership or familial relationship prevents qisas.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author says 'li ma rawayna' (due to what we narrated) and also provides a rational argument: qisas would benefit the owner, and one cannot impose punishment on oneself. Identify both the naqli (narrated) and aqli (rational) proofs.
The naqli proof is referenced but not quoted; the aqli proof is explained in the text.
3
Understand the reasoning: ownership and indivisibility
Analyze why ownership bars qisas: if the owner kills his slave, the qisas would be for himself (since the slave is his property), which is legally impossible. Then, for partial ownership, the principle of indivisibility (la yatajazzā) is applied – since qisas cannot be partially executed, it drops entirely.
This principle is unique to Hanafi fiqh and is based on the idea that qisas is a single, indivisible punishment.
4
Distinguish from other penalties
Note that qisas dropping does not mean no liability at all. The killer may still be liable for diyah (blood money) or tazir (discretionary punishment). The passage focuses solely on qisas.
This distinction is important to avoid misunderstanding – qisas is not the only consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبعبده ومدبره ومكاتبه كالأب وبعبده ومدبره ومكاتبه وبعبد ولده وبعبد ملك بعضه وإن ورث قصاصاً على أبيه سقط وإنما يقتص بالسيف مكاتب قتل عمداً وترك وفاء ووارثه سيده فقط أو لم) يعني لا يقتل بهؤلاء لما روينا ولأنه لو وجب القصاص لوجب له كما إذا قتله غيره ولا يجوز له أن يوجب على نفسه عقوبة. وكذا لا يستوجب ولده القصاص عليه لما بينا والقصاص لا يتجزئ فيسقط في البعض لأجل أنه ملك البعض فيسقط في الكل لعدم التجزئ. قال رحمه الله : (وإن ورث قصاصاً على أبيه سقط) لما ذكرنا أن الابن لا يستوجب العقوبة على أبيه وصورة المسألة فيما إذا قتل الأب أخ امرأته ثم ماتت امرأته قبل أن يقتص به فإن ابنه يرث القصاص الذي لها على أبيه فسقط لما ذكرنا كما إذا قتل امرأته وليس لها ابن إلا أنها منه فيسقط القصاص.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And for his slave, his mudabbar, his mukatab, like the father, and for his slave, his mudabbar, his mukatab, and for his son's slave, and for a slave of which he owns a part; and if he inherits qisas against his father, it drops; and qisas is only executed with the sword. (For a) mukatab who committed intentional murder and left insufficient funds, and his heir is only his master, or not.' Meaning: he is not killed for these, due to what we narrated, and because if qisas were obligatory, it would be obligatory for him (i.e., the owner) as if someone else killed him, and it is not allowed for him to impose punishment on himself. Likewise, his son does not deserve qisas against him, as we explained. Qisas is indivisible; it falls for a part because he owns a part, so it falls entirely due to lack of divisibility. He said: 'And if he inherits qisas against his father, it drops' due to what we mentioned, that the son does not deserve punishment against his father. The example: if the father kills his wife's brother, then his wife dies before qisas is executed, his son inherits the qisas right that she had against his father; it drops as we mentioned, just as if he killed his wife and she has no son except from him, qisas drops.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage addresses qisas cases involving slaves and ownership. It states that a person is not killed for killing his own slave, mudabbar (slave promised freedom upon owner's death), mukatab (slave under contract to earn freedom), his son's slave, or a slave he partially owns. The reason is that if qisas were imposed, it would be for the benefit of the owner himself (since the slave is his property), and one cannot impose a punishment on oneself. Also, qisas is indivisible; if the owner owns part of the slave, qisas for that partial ownership is impossible, so it drops entirely. The passage also covers the scenario where a son inherits a right to qisas against his father: if a father kills his wife's relative, then the wife dies, her son (who is also the father's son) inherits her qisas right against the father, but it drops because a son cannot have qisas against his father. This is similar to a father killing his wife who has no son except from him, where qisas also drops.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose owner has declared that he will be free upon the owner's death.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has a contract (kitaba) with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments.
لا يتجزئ (la yatajazzā): Qisas is indivisible; it cannot be applied partially, so if partial ownership prevents full qisas, it drops entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason qisas drops when a person kills a slave he partially owns?
A) The slave is not a full human being.
B) Qisas is indivisible and cannot be partially applied.
C) The owner can choose to pay diyah instead.
D) The other co-owner does not demand qisas.

Key Takeaway
Ownership of the victim (even partial) or a familial relationship prevents qisas because qisas cannot be applied to oneself or partially, and a son cannot execute qisas against his father.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
6 min
Mode of Executing Qisas and Heirs' Right
Ruling on mode of qisas and heirs' right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the execution of qisas and explain the Shafi'i counterargument, and identify the heirs' entitlement to qisas and diyah.

Core Idea
Qisas is executed only with a weapon, not in kind, and the right belongs to the heirs.

This lesson examines two related issues: the method of executing qisas (retaliation) and who is entitled to it. The Hanafi school, based on a hadith, holds that qisas must be carried out with a sword or any weapon, contrary to the Shafi'i view of retaliation in kind. The lesson also clarifies that the right to demand qisas or diyah belongs to the heirs of the victim.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on qisas execution
Identify the core ruling: qisas is executed only with the sword (or any weapon). This is the Hanafi position.
The ruling is about the mode of execution, not obligation.
2
Understand the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qisas should be executed in kind, using the same method as the murder, if that method is permissible. If the method is impermissible (like sodomy), a substitute is used.
This is based on qiyas (analogy) to retaliation in kind.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'لا قود إلا بالسيف' (No qisas except with the sword). The Companions understood 'sword' as any weapon. This is a clear text (nass) that restricts execution to the sword/weapon.
The hadith is explicit and cannot be overridden by qiyas.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The text refutes the Shafi'i view by arguing that the hadith is clear and that qiyas cannot override it. It also addresses the story of the Jew, suggesting it was about highway robbery, not regular qisas, and that any method may be used for muharibun.
The hadith abrogated earlier practices like mutilation.
5
Discuss the heirs' entitlement
The right to execute qisas or receive diyah belongs to the heirs of the victim, just as they inherit property. The diyah is initially considered a right of the deceased to cover debts and bequests, then passes to heirs by inheritance according to Abu Hanifa.
The passage cuts off, but the principle is clear: heirs are the entitled parties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإنما يقتص بالسيف) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : يقتص بمثل ما قتل إن قتله بفعل مشروع وإن قتله بغير فعل مشروع كلواطة يتخذ له خشبة ويفعل به كما فعل ولنا ما رواه سفيان من قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا قود إلا بالسيف»(۱) وهو نص على نفي استيفاء القود بغير السيف فكيف يلحق به دلالة ما كان سلاحاً من غير السيف؟ وهل يتصور أنه يدل كلام واحد على نفي شي وإثباته معاً؟ والحق أن يكون المراد بالسيف في الحديث المزبور السلاح مطلقاً بطريق الكناية كما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله «والمراد به السلاح». وصرح به صاحب الكافي والكفاية حيث قالا : ولنا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا قود إلا بالسيف (۱) والمراد بالسيف السلاح هكذا فهمت الصحابة رضي الله تعالى عنهم. وقال في النهاية : فإن قيل يحتمل أن يكون المراد من الحديث لا قود يجب إلا بالسيف لا أن يكون معناه لا قود يستوفي إلا بالسيف قلنا القود اسم لفعل . هو جزاء القتل دون ما يجب شرعاً وإن حمل عليه كان مجازاً، ولأن القود قد يجب بغير السيف كالقتل بالنار والإبرة فلم يمكن حمله عليه لوجود وجوب القود بدون القتل بالسيف وإنما السيف مخصوص : بالاستيفاء اهـ. وما رواه كان مشروعاً ثم نسخ كما نسخت المثلة أو يكون اليهودي ساعياً في الأرض بالفساد فيقتل كما يراه الإمام ليكون أردع وهذا هو الظاهر ، ولأن اليهودي كان أخذ المال ألا ترى إلى ما روي في الخبر عن أنس بن مالك أنه قال : عدا يهودي على جارية فأخذها بما معها الحديث. وهذا شأن قطاع الطريق وهذا يقتل بأي شاء الإمام ويؤيد هذا المعنى ما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قتل اليهودي بخلاف ما كان قتل به الجارية . والاستيفاء إما أن يكون بحكم الإرث أو الملك أو بحكم السلطنة والولاية، والمستحق للقصاص والدية الورثة مثل ما يستحق ماله على فرائض الله تعالى يدخل في ذلك الزوج والزوجة، والوارث يقوم مقام المورث في استحقاق كل ما كان له من الأملاك والحقوق إلا أن الدية تجب حقاً للميت ابتداء حتى نقضي منها ديونه وننفذ وصاياه ثم تثبت للورثة بطريق الخلافة والوراثة عند أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه حتى لو أقام واحد من الورثة البينة على
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And qisas is only executed with the sword.' And al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Qisas is executed with the like of what he killed with, if he killed with a permissible act; if he killed with an impermissible act, like sodomy, a piece of wood is taken and done to him as he did. Our proof is what Sufyan narrated from his statement, peace be upon him: 'No qisas except with the sword.' It is a clear text negating execution of qisas with other than the sword, so how can the indication of a weapon other than the sword be attached to it? Can a single statement indicate both negation and affirmation simultaneously? The truth is that what is meant by 'sword' in the said hadith is any weapon by way of metonymy, as the author pointed out by saying 'and the intended meaning is any weapon.' The author of al-Kafi and al-Kifayah explicitly said: Our proof is his statement, peace be upon him: 'No qisas except with the sword' and the intended meaning of 'sword' is the weapon; this is how the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, understood it. And in al-Nihayah, it is said: If it is objected that the hadith might mean 'No qisas is obligatory except with the sword,' not that it is executed only with the sword, we say: 'al-qawad' is a noun for the act of retaliation itself, not for what is obligatory legally; if it is interpreted that way, it is metaphorical. Also, qisas may be obligated without the sword, like killing by fire or a needle, so it is not possible to restrict the hadith to obligation, because qisas can be obligated without killing by sword; the sword is only specified for execution. That which was narrated (about the Jew) was lawful then abrogated, as mutilation was abrogated, or it may be that the Jew was a rebel causing corruption, so he was killed as the Imam sees fit for deterrence, and this is the apparent view. The Jew took money, as is seen in the hadith of Anas ibn Malik: a Jew attacked a slave-girl and took what she had... This is the case of highway robbers, and he is killed by whatever the Imam wishes. This meaning is supported by the report that the Prophet, peace be upon him, killed the Jew contrary to the way he killed the slave-girl. The execution is either by virtue of inheritance, ownership, or by virtue of authority and jurisdiction. Those entitled to qisas and diyah are the heirs, just as they are entitled to his property according to the divine shares of inheritance. This includes the husband and wife. The heir stands in the place of the deceased in entitlement to all his possessions and rights, except that the diyah is initially a right of the deceased, so we pay his debts and execute his bequests from it, then it is confirmed for the heirs by way of succession and inheritance according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, such that if one of the heirs establishes proof...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is divided into two main discussions. First, the ruling that qisas is executed only with the sword. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that qisas should be executed in kind, using the same method as the murder, if that method is permissible (e.g., stabbing). The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'No qisas except with the sword,' which the Companions understood as meaning any weapon, not literally only a sword. The text refutes the Shafi'i view by arguing that the hadith is clear in restricting execution to the sword (or weapon), and other methods are not allowed. Exception is made for highway robbers (muharibun), where the Imam may choose the method. Then the passage shifts to who is entitled to execute qisas: the heirs of the victim, who also inherit the right to diyah (blood money). The diyah is initially due to the deceased to pay off debts and bequests, then goes to heirs. The text begins an example about one heir establishing proof, but it is cut off.

Key Terms
القود (al-qawad): The act of executing qisas (retaliation) by killing the killer.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): The execution or exacting of the penalty (qisas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) As meaning qisas is only obligatory when a sword is used
D) As abrogated by later practice

Key Takeaway
Qisas is executed only with a sword/weapon, not in kind, and the right belongs to the heirs.

Qisas — Retaliation

Ruling: Certain Persons Not Subject to Qisas
States exempt persons with transmitted and rational proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of persons who are not subject to qisas in Hanafi law and explain the reasoning based on textual evidence and the indivisibility principle.

Core Idea
A father is not killed for his child, and a master is not killed for his slave — qisas is indivisible and cannot be imposed for one's own benefit.

The principle of qisas (retaliation) is a cornerstone of Islamic criminal law, but not every intentional killing triggers the death penalty. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists specific individuals—such as a father or a master—who are exempt from qisas when killing someone under their authority. Understanding these exceptions requires both transmitted proof and a rational understanding of how qisas operates.

Guided Path
1
List the exempt categories
Identify the six categories mentioned: the father (al-ab), his slave (abdihi), his mudabbar, his mukatab, his son's slave (abd waladihi), and a slave partially owned by the killer (malik al-ba'd).
The list appears exhaustive in the text.
2
Examine the transmitted proof
The text cites a narration (riwaya) — the hadith 'La yuqtalu walidun bi waladihi' — as the primary textual evidence for the father's exemption.
This is a zanni al-thubut hadith, but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the rational proof (talil)
The passage gives a rational argument: if qisas were obligatory, it would be for the benefit of the killer himself (since the victim is in his ownership/authority), and a person cannot impose a punishment on himself.
This argument reinforces the textual evidence.
4
Apply the indivisibility rule to partial ownership
When the killer partially owns the victim, qisas is not applied because qisas is indivisible; it drops entirely rather than being partially applied.
This is a Hanafi specific rule: al-qisas la yatajazzi'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالأب وبعبده ومدبره ومكاتبه وبعبد ولده وبعبد ملك بعضه يعني لا يقتل بهؤلاء لما روينا ولأنه لو وجب القصاص لوجب له كما إذا قتله غيره ولا يجوز له أن يوجب على نفسه عقوبة. وكذا لا يستوجب ولده القصاص عليه لما بينا والقصاص لا يتجزئ فيسقط في البعض لأجل أنه ملك البعض فيسقط في الكل لعدم التجزئ.
Like the father, his slave, his mudabbar, his mukatab, his son's slave, and a slave partially owned. Meaning: he is not killed for these, due to what we narrated, and because if qisas were obligatory, it would be obligatory for him (the killer himself), as if another had killed him; and he cannot impose a punishment on himself. Likewise, his son does not deserve qisas against him due to what we explained. Qisas is indivisible, so it falls in part because he owns part, thus it falls entirely due to indivisibility.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanded by the commentator. It lists persons who are not subject to qisas if they kill someone under their authority: a father killing his child, a master killing his slave (whether absolute, mudabbar, or mukatab), and a person killing his son's slave, or a slave partially owned by him. The reasoning is twofold: first, transmitted evidence (riwaya); second, rational: if qisas were obligatory, it would be for the benefit of the killer himself (since the victim is his property or under his authority), and a person cannot impose a punishment on himself. Additionally, the son does not have qisas against his father. The rule about partial ownership is explained: because qisas is indivisible, if the killer partially owns the victim, qisas drops entirely. This is a Hanafi position based on the principle that qisas cannot be divided.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or injury, specifically the death penalty for intentional killing.
ملك البعض (malik al-ba'd): Partial ownership of a slave, where the killer owns some portion of the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does qisas drop when the killer partially owns the victim?
A) Because the killer is not a sane adult.
B) Because qisas is indivisible, so it falls entirely.
C) Because the victim is not a Muslim.
D) Because the killing was unintentional.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts fathers, masters, and related persons from qisas based on a hadith and the principle that qisas is indivisible and cannot be imposed for one's own benefit.

Inheriting Qisas Against One's Father: Why It Drops
Explains that inheriting qisas against one's father drops the right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that inheriting a right of qisas against one's own father causes the right to drop, and explain the underlying principle and its application to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A son cannot demand qisas against his father, even if he inherits the right from his mother.

In Hanafi law, the right to qisas (retaliatory punishment) can be inherited like property. However, there is a fundamental restriction: a son may not seek qisas against his own father. This lesson examines a specific case where a son inherits a qisas right against his father through his mother, and explains why the right immediately drops. Understanding this rule illustrates how Islamic law balances justice with family sanctity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Inherited Right
Recognize that in the scenario, the son inherits the right of qisas from his deceased mother, who had a claim against her husband (the son's father) for killing her brother.
The inheritance of qisas is a Hanafi position; other schools may treat it differently.
2
Apply the Son-Father Relationship
Recall the principle that a descendant cannot exact qisas against an ascendant. The son is the father's child, so the right to qisas is blocked.
This is derived from the general rule that a child cannot cause the death of a parent in retaliation.
3
Determine the Consequence
The qisas right drops (sāqiṭ) immediately upon inheritance. It does not transfer to the son in a way that he can execute it.
The right is not simply suspended; it is extinguished.
4
Compare with a Similar Case
The text mentions another scenario: if a man kills his wife and she has no son except from him, the son inherits but qisas also drops. Recognize the consistency.
In both cases, the heir is the killer's son, so the result is the same.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ورث قصاصاً على أبيه سقط لما ذكرنا أن الابن لا يستوجب العقوبة على أبيه وصورة المسألة فيما إذا قتل الأب أخ امرأته ثم ماتت امرأته قبل أن يقتص به فإن ابنه يرث القصاص الذي لها على أبيه فسقط لما ذكرنا كما إذا قتل امرأته وليس لها ابن إلا أنها منه فيسقط القصاص.
And if he inherits qisas against his father, it drops, due to what we mentioned that the son does not deserve punishment on his father. The example: if a father kills his wife's brother, then his wife dies before qisas is executed, her son (the killer's son) inherits her right of qisas against his own father; it drops as we said, just as if he killed his wife and she has no son except from him, then qisas drops.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This is an application of the previous principle: a son cannot have qisas against his father. The commentator gives a scenario: a man kills his brother-in-law (his wife's brother). The wife had a right of qisas against her husband. If she dies before executing it, her son (who is also the killer's son) inherits that right. However, since the heir is the son of the killer, the qisas right drops immediately. Similarly, if a man kills his wife and she has no children except from him, the son inherits but cannot execute against his father.

Key Terms
وراثة القصاص (wirathat al-qisas): The inheritance of the right to demand qisas from the deceased victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example given in the passage, why does the inherited qisas drop?
A) Because the son is a minor.
B) Because the killer is the son's father.
C) Because the son already pardoned the killer.
D) Because the victim was not a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A son cannot inherit and execute a right of qisas against his own father; the right drops immediately to maintain family harmony and respect for parents.

Qisas — Retaliation
